## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves relating mechanical stress (sigma) to strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is a classic problem in solid mechanics and materials science. The relationship captures how material deformation behavior (elastic, plastic, viscoelastic) depends on both strain level and temperature.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': "Hooke's law (linear elastic)", 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon', 'scenario': 'Linear elastic regime at constant temperature'}
- {'name': "Temperature-dependent Hooke's law", 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T)', 'scenario': 'Linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus'}
- {'name': 'Power-law hardening (Ramberg-Osgood style)', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon ** c1', 'scenario': 'Nonlinear stress-strain relationship in plastic deformation'}
- {'name': 'Temperature-dependent power-law', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon ** c1 * T ** c2', 'scenario': 'Combined strain hardening and thermal softening'}
- {'name': 'Johnson-Cook type model (simplified)', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon ** c2) * (1 + c3 * T)', 'scenario': 'Flow stress with strain hardening and linear thermal softening'}
- {'name': 'Exponential thermal softening', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T)', 'scenario': 'Elastic modulus decreasing exponentially with temperature'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial stress-strain with temperature', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon ** 2 + c2 * T', 'scenario': 'Quadratic stress-strain with additive thermal stress'}
- {'name': 'Thermal stress offset', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * (T + c2)', 'scenario': 'Linear elasticity with thermal expansion stress contribution'}
- {'name': 'Voce hardening with temperature', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T)', 'scenario': 'Saturating hardening with exponential thermal softening'}
- {'name': 'Hyperbolic sine creep law (Garofalo)', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T)', 'scenario': 'High-temperature creep/deformation with sinh dependence'}
- {'name': 'Homologous temperature softening (Johnson-Cook style)', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon ** c2) * (1 - (c3 * T) ** c4)', 'scenario': 'Flow stress with power-law thermal softening'}
- {'name': 'Cubic stress-strain', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon ** 2 + c2 * epsilon ** 3', 'scenario': 'Nonlinear elasticity (rubber-like or hyperelastic materials)'}
- {'name': 'Arrhenius-type thermal activation with strain', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon ** c1 * exp(c2 / T)', 'scenario': 'Thermally activated deformation (dislocation glide)'}
- {'name': 'Bilinear with temperature coupling', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon * T + c1 * epsilon + c2 * T + c3', 'scenario': 'Full linear interaction model between strain and temperature'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor on strain term that decreases with T: epsilon * f(T) where f is decreasing
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating asymptotic stress plateau
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) multiplicative factors
- Nonlinear elasticity → Odd-power polynomial in epsilon (epsilon, epsilon**3, epsilon**5) for symmetric tension-compression
- Thermal expansion / residual stress → Additive terms linear or polynomial in T independent of strain
- Yield stress with hardening → Additive constant c0 + hardening function of epsilon, representing initial yield plus work hardening
- Strain-temperature cross-coupling → Product terms epsilon*T indicating that temperature modifies the effective stiffness
- Phase transition or material instability → Non-monotonic dependence on T (e.g., quadratic in T with sign change)

Now let me reconsider. Maybe I should look at candidates that have the right structure more carefully.

The GT has three terms:
1. `A*epsilon**3` (A is a constant)
2. `B*epsilon**(1/5)*exp(D/T)` (B, D constants)
3. `C*T*epsilon**3` (C constant)

Terms 1 and 3 combine to `(A + C*T)*epsilon**3`.

The key structural elements are:
- `epsilon**3` (or `epsilon**c` with c=3)
- `epsilon**(1/5)*exp(negative_const/T)` 
- `T*epsilon**3`

These are three linearly independent basis functions. Any matching candidate must contain all three.

Let me check if any candidate I might have missed has `T*epsilon**3`:

Looking through all candidates again for `T*epsilon**3` or equivalent:
- Candidates with `T*c*(c+epsilon)**3`: 7, 82
- Candidates with `T*c*(c+epsilon)**4`: 8, 32
- Candidates with `T*epsilon**5`: 37
- Candidates with `T*epsilon*exp(c*epsilon)`: 6, 9, 19, 26, 35, 40, 44, 45, 50, 52, 56, 57, 71, 76, 77, 78, 88, 92, 107, 108, 122, 134, 145
- Candidates with `T*epsilon`: 27, 73, 87, 90, 91, 105, 117, 142
- Candidates with `T` (no epsilon): 1, 2, 5, 7, 13, 18, 29, 34, 46, 48, 49, 51, 58, 63, 74, 111, 112, 119, 131, 141, 148, 149, 150, 155
- Candidates with `T**c0`: 13, 29, 59, 104, 133

None of these directly have `T*epsilon**3` except through expansion of `(c+epsilon)**3` or `(c+epsilon)**4`.

For Candidate 7: `T*c0 + T*c1*(c2 + epsilon)**3 + c3*epsilon**(1/5) + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**2`

Expanding: `T*c0 + T*c1*(c2**3 + 3*c2**2*epsilon + 3*c2*epsilon**2 + epsilon**3) + c3*epsilon**(1/5) + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**2`

= `T*(c0 + c1*c2**3) + T*c1*3*c2**2*epsilon + T*c1*3*c2*epsilon**2 + T*c1*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon**(1/5) + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**2`

If c2=0: `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon**(1/5) + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**2`

GT needs: `A*epsilon**3 + B*T*epsilon**3 + C*epsilon**(1/5)*exp(D/T)`

Candidate 7 with c2=0 gives: `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon**(1/5) + c4*epsilon + c5*epsilon**2`

Setting c4=0, c5=0: `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon**(1/5)`

GT: `A*epsilon**3 + B*T*epsilon**3 + C*epsilon**(1/5)*exp(D/T)`

Candidate 7 has `T*c0` (linear in T, no epsilon) but GT doesn't have a pure T term.
Candidate 7 has `c3*epsilon**(1/5)` but GT has `C*epsilon**(1/5)*exp(D/T)`.
Candidate 7 has `T*c1*epsilon**3` ✓ but is missing `epsilon**3` (without T).

Even if we keep c4, c5 nonzero, we get polynomial terms in epsilon but no `epsilon**3` without T, and no `exp(c/T)`. [NO MATCH]

For Candidate 82: `T*c0*(c1 + epsilon)**3 + c2*epsilon**c3`

With c1=0: `T*c0*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon**c3`

Setting c3=1/5: `T*c0*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon**(1/5)`

This has `T*epsilon**3` and `epsilon**(1/5)` but is missing `epsilon**3` and `exp(c/T)`. [NO MATCH]

With c1≠0: We get `T*c0*(c1**3 + 3c1**2*epsilon + 3c1*epsilon**2 + epsilon**3) + c2*epsilon**c3`

This gives `T*epsilon**3` but also `T*epsilon**2`, `T*epsilon`, `T` which can't be zeroed without zeroing `T*epsilon**3`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 148:** `T*c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon**3`

Has `T`, `epsilon**c2`, `epsilon`, `epsilon**2`, `epsilon**3`. Setting c2=1/5: `T*c0 + c1*epsilon**(1/5) + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon**3`. Missing `T*epsilon**3` and `exp(c/T)`. [NO MATCH]

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider **Candidate 53** more carefully:

`c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*exp(T*c3) + c4*(c5 + c6*epsilon**c7)*(T*c8 + 1)`

= `c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*exp(T*c3) + c4*c5*T*c8 + c4*c5 + c4*c6*epsilon**c7*T*c8 + c4*c6*epsilon**c7`

Setting c3=0 (so exp(0)=1): `c0*epsilon**c1 + c2 + c4*c5*T*c8 + c4*c5 + c4*c6*c8*T*epsilon**c7 + c4*c6*epsilon**c7`

= `c0*epsilon**c1 + (c2 + c4*c5) + c4*c5*c8*T + c4*c6*c8*T*epsilon**c7 + c4*c6*epsilon**c7`

Setting c7=3, c1=1/5: 
= `c0*epsilon**(1/5) + const + A*T + B*T*epsilon**3 + C*epsilon**3`

This has `T*epsilon**3` ✓ and `epsilon**3` ✓ and `epsilon**(1/5)` but NOT `epsilon**(1/5)*exp(c/T)`. The `epsilon**(1/5)` term has no `exp(c/T)` factor. Also has unwanted `T` term.

GT needs `epsilon**(1/5)*exp(c/T)` which is fundamentally different from `epsilon**(1/5)`. [NO MATCH]

Already analyzed. [NO MATCH]

2. Through products: something like `epsilon**3 * (T*c + d)` which gives `T*c*epsilon**3 + d*epsilon**3`

Let me check if any candidate has `epsilon**c * (T*a + b)` structure:

**Candidate 53:** Has `c4*(c5 + c6*epsilon**c7)*(T*c8 + 1)` which expands to include `T*epsilon**c7`. But no `exp(c/T)`.

OK, I've now exhaustively checked all 155 candidates. None of them can produce the required combination of basis functions: `epsilon**3`, `T*epsilon**3`, and `epsilon**(1/5)*exp(c/T)`.

Let me do one final sanity check on a few promising-looking candidates:

**Candidate 6:** `T*c0*epsilon*exp(c1*epsilon) + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5*exp(c6/T)`

This has `exp(c6/T)` ✓. Setting c5=1/5: `c4*epsilon**(1/5)*exp(c6/T)` ✓.

For the remaining terms: `T*c0*epsilon*exp(c1*epsilon) + c2*epsilon**c3`

We need these to equal `A*epsilon**3 + B*T*epsilon**3`.

`c2*epsilon**c3` with c3=3 gives `c2*epsilon**3` ✓ for the `A*epsilon**3` part.

But `T*c0*epsilon*exp(c1*epsilon)` needs to equal `B*T*epsilon**3`.

This means `c0*epsilon*exp(c1*epsilon) = B*epsilon**3`, i.e., `c0*exp(c1*epsilon) = B*epsilon**2`.

But `exp(c1*epsilon)` is an exponential function and `epsilon**2` is a polynomial. These can NEVER be equal for all epsilon (unless c1=0, but then `c0 = B*epsilon**2` which is impossible for a constant c0). [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `c0*epsilon**(1/5)*exp(c1/T) + c2 + c3*epsilon**5 + c4*epsilon**c5*exp(c6/T)`

Two terms with `exp(c/T)`: `c0*epsilon**(1/5)*exp(c1/T)` and `c4*epsilon**c5*exp(c6/T)`.

If c1=c6 (same exponential factor): `(c0*epsilon**(1/5) + c4*epsilon**c5)*exp(c1/T) + c2 + c3*epsilon**5`

GT has `C*epsilon**(1/5)*exp(D/T)` as one term. The other terms `A*epsilon**3 + B*T*epsilon**3` have no `exp(c/T)`.

So we'd need `c4*epsilon**c5*exp(c6/T)` to somehow produce `T*epsilon**3`. But `exp(c6/T)` is NOT `T`. [NO MATCH]

If c1≠c6: We have two different exponentials in 1/T. GT only has one such exponential. The other GT terms (`epsilon**3`, `T*epsilon**3`) don't involve `exp(c/T)`. So we'd need one of the `exp(c/T)` terms to vanish (set c0=0 or c4=0), leaving us with only one `exp(c/T)` term plus `c2 + c3*epsilon**5`. This can't produce `T*epsilon**3`. [NO MATCH]

I'm now fully confident: **none of the 155 candidates match the GT**.
